
Extraído de: http://systemmanager.ru/win2k_regestry.en/

                                              ===================                                               
============================================== HKEY_CURRENT_USER ===============================================
                                              ===================                                               

 HKCU

Description:

 The HKEY_CURRENT_USER subtree contains the user profile for the user who is currently logged on to the
 computer. The user profile includes environment variables, personal program groups, desktop settings,
 network connections, printers, and application preferences. The data in the user profile is similar
 to the data stored in the Win.ini file in Windows 3.x.

 The HKEY_CURRENT USER subtree does not contain any data. It just stores a pointer to the content of HKEY_USERS\<Security
 ID (SID) of current user>. As such, the data stored in this subkey of HKEY_USERS appears in HKEY_CURRENT_USER.
 The data can be viewed and changed directly and programmatically in either location.

 A new HKEY_CURRENT_USER subtree is created each time a user logs on. The data for HKEY_CURRENT_USER comes
 from the profile of the current user. If no profile is available, HKEY_CURRENT_USER is built from the
 user profile settings established for a default user, stored on the System drive\Documents and Settings\Default
 User (WINNT)\Ntuser.dat.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Software ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\

Description:

 The Software subkey stores program variables that are specific to the current user. The system stores
 some of its variables in the subkeys in Software. In addition, the Software subkey contains subkeys
 representing the vendors that produced the software running on the system, including Microsoft.

Related Entries:

 Software subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                  ===========                                                   
================================================== Microsoft ===================================================
                                                  ===========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\

Description:

 The Microsoft subkey stores configuration data for Microsoft programs running on the computer. The subkeys
 in the Microsoft subkey represent each of the programs. The entries in the program subkeys are specific
 to the current user.

 The Microsoft subkey in HKEY_CURRENT_USER stores entries that apply only to the current user of the computer.
 There is also a Software\Microsoft subkey in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE which stores entries that apply to all
 users of the computer.

Related Entries:

 Microsoft subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   =========                                                    
=================================================== Windows ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\

Description:

 The Windows subkey stores configuration data for the programs running on the Win32 subsystem. The subkeys
 of the Windows subkey represent versions of the Win32 subsystem, such as CurrentVersion. Each version
 subkey contains subkeys representing programs that run on that version of the subsystem.

 The Windows subkey in HKEY_CURRENT_USER stores entries that apply only to the current user of the computer.
 There is also a SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows subkey in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE that stores entries that apply
 to all users of the computer.

Related Entries:

 Windows subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

================================================= Windows Help =================================================
                                                 ==============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\

Description:

 The values in this subkey are not used by and have no effect on Windows 2000.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\

                                                ================                                                
================================================ CurrentVersion ================================================
                                                ================                                                

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\

Description:

 The CurrentVersion subkey stores configuration data for programs running on the Win32 subsystem. The
 subkeys of CurrentVersion represent programs that run on the current version of Win32 subsystem and
 store user-specific configuration data for those programs.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Explorer ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\

Description:

 The Explorer subkey stores configuration data for Windows Explorer and the Windows interface, including
 the Start menu, the desktop, common folders, and Control Panel.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Policies ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\

Description:

 The Policies subkey contains entries that store Group Policy settings.

 Group Policy adds, deletes, and changes the values of entries in this subkey when you use the Group Policy
 snap-in to configure a policy, that is, to enable or disable the policy. When the policies affecting
 you or your computer change, such as when you move to a new user group, Group Policy deletes the entries
 applied to the old group and then adds the entries applied to the new group.

 Group Policy manages registry entries in four Policies subkeys:

 The Policies subkeys in HKCU store policy-related entries that are configured separately for each user.
 The system adds these entries when you enable (and, for some policies, when you disable) a policy in
 the User Configuration folder in Group Policy.

 The Policies subkeys in HKLM store policy-related entries that apply to all users of the computer. The
 system adds these entries when you enable (and, for some policies, when you disable) a policy in the
 Computer Configuration folder in Group Policy.

 Many policy-related entries can appear in both HKCU and HKLM. Typically, the entries in HKLM take precedence
 over the entries in HKCU when both are configured.

 The SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies subkey stores policy-related entries for Windows 2000
 and for Windows NT 4.0 and earlier. The SOFTWARE\Policies subkey is new in Windows 2000. Please note
 that the different versions of Windows support different policies.

Change method:

 To add, remove, or change the value of entries in this subkey, use Group Policy.

 Note

 Many of the entries in the Policies subkeys have counterparts in other registry subkeys. These counterparts,
 known as preferences have the same effect on user or computer features as entries in the Policies subkey.
 However, when an entry appears in the Policies subkey, the preference is almost always ignored. For
 details, see the entry descriptions.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

 Caution

 Do not use a registry editor to change the values in this subkey. If you do, they will be overwritten
 the next time your policies are refreshed.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Advanced ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\

Description:

 The Advanced subkey stores the settings of options on the Taskbar and Start Menu Properties dialog box.

Change method:

 To change the value of entries in this subkey, use the Taskbar and Start Menu Properties dialog box.
 Do not edit the registry.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                ================                                                
================================================ DesktopProcess ================================================
                                                ================                                                

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Determines whether the components of Windows 2000 Explorer run in a single process or in two separate
 processes.

┌───────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                  Meaning                                   │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │ All of the components of Windows Explorer (Explorer, Desktop, and Taskbar) │
│       │ run as separate threads in a single, multithreaded process called Explorer.exe. │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │  All instances of Windows Explorer run in one process and the Desktop and  │
│       │ Taskbar run in a separate process. Both processes are called Explorer.exe. │
└───────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Note

 Windows 2000 does not add this entry to the registry. You can add it by editing the registry or by using
 a program that edits the registry.

Tip:

 To verify that DesktopProcess is enabled, use the Processes tab in Task Manager. If the value of DesktopProcess
 is 1, at least two instances of the Explorer.exe process should appear in the list of processes (one
 for the Desktop and Taskbar and one for Windows Explorer). For each additional instance of Windows Explorer,
 a new instance of Explorer.exe should appear in the list of processes.

 Caution

 Enabling DesktopProcess can interfere with the functions of Windows Explorer if the computer is not equipped
 to run all processes efficiently. Do not set the value of DesktopProcess to 1 unless the computer has
 a Pentium processor (or equivalent) and at least 16 MB of physical random access memory.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                ===============                                                 
================================================ Shell Folders =================================================
                                                ===============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\

Description:

 The entries in the Shell Folders subkey are not used by and have no effect on Windows 2000. Paths to
 the Windows Explorer folders are stored in the User Shell Folders subkey. For more information on shell
 folders, search the Platform Software Development Kit (SDK) documentation in the MSDN Library at http://msdn.microsoft.com.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                               ==================                                               
=============================================== Shutdown Setting ===============================================
                                               ==================                                               

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────────────────────────────────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │               Range               │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────────────────────────────────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 1 | 2 | 4 | 8 | 10 | 20 | 40 | 80 │       2       │
└───────────┴───────────────────────────────────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Specifies the shutdown setting.

┌───────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                   Meaning                                    │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x1  │   Log off. Ends your session, leaving the computer running on full power.    │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x2  │   Shut down. Ends your session and shuts down Windows 2000 so that you can   │
│       │                            safely turn off power.                            │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x4  │ Restart. Ends your session, shuts down Windows 2000, and starts Windows 2000 │
│       │                                    again.                                    │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x8  │   Restart in MS-DOS mode. Ends your session, shuts down Windows 2000, and    │
│       │ starts MS-DOS mode. (Restart in MS-DOS mode is not available in Windows 2000) │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x10 │ Stand by. Maintains your session, keeping the computer running on low power  │
│       │ with data still in memory. (This setting requires power management hardware  │
│       │                                  support.)                                   │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x20 │   Stand by (with wakeup events disabled). Maintains your session, keeping    │
│       │  the computer running on low power with data still in memory. (This setting  │
│       │                 requires power management hardware support.)                 │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x40 │ Hibernate. Saves your session to disk so that you can safely turn off power. │
│       │        Your session is restored the next time you start Windows 2000.        │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  0x80 │   Disconnect. Disconnects your session. You can reconnect to this session    │
│       │   when you log on again. (Disconnect is available only in Terminal Server    │
│       │                                  sessions.)                                  │
└───────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 This value is maintained as the "last selection" for a given user. Windows 2000 writes this value whenever
 an option is selected from the shut down dialog.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                 ==============                                                 
================================================= IntelliMenus =================================================
                                                 ==============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\Advanced

┌───────────┬──────────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │  Range   │ Default value │
├───────────┼──────────┼───────────────┤
│   REG_SZ  │ YES | No │      YES      │
└───────────┴──────────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Enables and disables personalized menus.

 This entry stores the setting of the Use Personalized Menus check box on the Taskbar and Start Menu Properties
 dialog box.

 Windows 2000 personalizes long menus by moving recently used items to the top of the menu and by hiding
 items that have not been used recently. Users can display the hidden items by clicking an arrow to extend
 the menu.

┌───────┬──────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │           Meaning            │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────┤
│  YES  │ Enables personalized menus.  │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────┤
│   No  │ Disables personalized menus. │
└───────┴──────────────────────────────┘

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, click Start, click Settings, click Taskbar & Start Menu. This entry
 corresponds to the Use Personalized Menus check box on the General tab of the Taskbar and Start Menu
 Properties dialog box. Do not edit the registry.

 Note

 This entry can be superceded by a policy included in Windows 2000. While the Disable Personalized Menus
 policy is in effect, the system removes the Use Personalized Menus check box from the Start Menu and
 ignores this entry. The setting of the Disable Personalized Menus policy is stored in the value of Intellimenus
 in the Policies subkey. If users cannot find the Use Personalized Menus option, check the setting of
 the Disable personalized menus policy.

 Personalized menus require user tracking. If the Disable user tracking policy is in effect, Group Policy
 sets the value of NoInstrumentation to 1. As a result, the system disables user tracking and personalized
 menus and ignores the value of Intellimenus.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policies, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm) on
 the Windows 2000 Resource Kit CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

Related Entries:

 Intellimenus (Policies subkey)

 NoInstrumentation

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                     ======                                                     
===================================================== Show =====================================================
                                                     ======                                                     

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\Tips

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       1       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Determines whether the Welcome to Windows splash screen, Welcome.exe, is shown the next time the user
 logs on.

┌───────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                  Meaning                                  │
├───────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │  The Welcome to Windows splash screen will not be shown the next time the │
│       │                               user logs on.                               │
├───────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │ The Welcome to Windows splash screen will be shown the next time the user │
│       │                                  logs on.                                 │
└───────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry for the current user, use the Show this screen at startup check box
 on the splash screen.

 Note

 This entry can be overridden by a Group Policy. When the Don't display welcome screen at logon policy
 in the User Configuration or Computer Configuration folders is enabled, this entry is ignored. Users
 can display the welcome screen manually, but the system does not display it at logon, regardless of
 the setting of the Show this screen at startup check box. The Don't display welcome screen at logon
 policy setting is stored in NoWelcomeScreen (HKLM) and NoWelcomeScreen (HKCU).

 This entry affects Windows 2000nbsp;Professional only.

Tip:

 If a user's Welcome screen does not appear as expected, check the setting of the Don't display welcome
 screen at logon policy. This policy takes preference over the user setting and the value of this entry.

Related Entries:

 NoWelcomeScreen (HKLM)

 NoWelcomeScreen (HKCU)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                                   =========                                                    
=================================================== AppData ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\User Shell Folders

┌───────────────┬───────┬────────────────────────────────┐
│   Data type   │ Range │         Default value          │
├───────────────┼───────┼────────────────────────────────┤
│ REG_EXPAND_SZ │  Path │ %USERPROFILE%\Application Data │
└───────────────┴───────┴────────────────────────────────┘

Description:

 Stores the path to a folder containing user-specific files installed by applications.

 For example, Microsoft Word can install a custom dictionary in the location specified by the value of
 this entry. You can enter any valid UNC name or mapped drive in the value of this entry.

 Note

 The %USERPROFILE% variable represents the path to the user's profile folder. The default is Systemroot\Documents
 and Settings\<username>.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

=================================================== Desktop ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\User Shell Folders

┌───────────────┬───────┬───────────────────────┐
│   Data type   │ Range │     Default value     │
├───────────────┼───────┼───────────────────────┤
│ REG_EXPAND_SZ │  Path │ %USERPROFILE%\Desktop │
└───────────────┴───────┴───────────────────────┘

Description:

 Stores the path to the folder containing the shortcuts and Internet addresses that appear on the user's
 desktop.

 You can enter any valid UNC name or mapped drive in the value of this entry.

 Note

 The %USERPROFILE% variable represents the path to the user's profile folder. The default is Systemroot\Documents
 and Settings\<username>.

Related Entries:

 Common Desktop in HKLM\User Shell Folders

=================================================== NetHood ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\User Shell Folders

│   Data type   │ Range │     Default value     │

└───────────────┴───────┴───────────────────────┘

 You can enter any valid UNC name or mapped drive in the value of this entry.

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Personal ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\User Shell Folders

┌───────────────┬───────┬────────────────────────────┐
│   Data type   │ Range │       Default value        │
├───────────────┼───────┼────────────────────────────┤
│ REG_EXPAND_SZ │  Path │ %USERPROFILE%\My Documents │
└───────────────┴───────┴────────────────────────────┘

Description:

 Stores the path to the user's Personal folder.

 The Personal folder is the default location for saving application files. You can enter any valid UNC
 name or mapped drive in the value of this entry.

 Note

 The %USERPROFILE% variable represents the path to the user's Profiles folder. The default is Systemroot\Documents
 and Settings\username.

Related Entries:

 Personal in HKLM\User Shell Folders

================================================== PrintHood ===================================================
                                                  ===========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\User Shell Folders

┌───────────────┬───────┬─────────────────────────┐
│   Data type   │ Range │      Default value      │
├───────────────┼───────┼─────────────────────────┤
│ REG_EXPAND_SZ │  Path │ %USERPROFILE%\PrintHood │
└───────────────┴───────┴─────────────────────────┘

Description:

 Stores the path to the folder containing shortcuts to printers that the user has added to the computer.

 You can enter any valid UNC name or mapped drive in the value of this entry.

 Note

 The %USERPROFILE% variable represents the path to the user's Profiles folder. The default is Systemroot\Documents
 and Settings\username.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Comdlg32 ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\

Description:

 The Comdlg32 subkey contains entries that store Group Policy settings for the common Open dialog box.
 The entries in this subkey are written and maintained by Group Policy and read and interpreted by the
 Open dialog box program.

 The entries in the Comdlg32 subkey only affect programs that use the standard Open dialog box provided
 to developers of Windows programs.

Tip:

 To see an example of the standard Open dialog box, run Notepad and, from the File menu, click Open.

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   ==========                                                   
=================================================== Explorer ===================================================
                                                   ==========                                                   

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\

Description:

 The Policies\Explorer subkey contains entries that store Group Policy settings for Windows Explorer and
 the Windows interface. These include policies for the Start menu, taskbar, desktop, and Control Panel.
 The entries in this subkey are written and maintained by Group Policy and read and interpreted by the
 Windows Explorer program.

 This subkey in HKEY_CURRENT_USER stores policy-related entries that are configured separately for each
 user. There is also a Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer subkey in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE
 that stores policy-related entries that apply to all users of this computer.

 Note

 Many of the entries in the Policies subkeys have counterparts in other registry subkeys. These counterparts,
 known as preferences have the same effect on user or computer features as entries in the Policies subkey.
 However, when an entry appears in the Policies subkey, the preference is almost always ignored. For
 details, see the entry descriptions.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 Explorer subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   =========                                                    
=================================================== Network ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\

Description:

 The Policies\Network subkey contains entries that store Group Policy settings for network services, such
 as Offline Files and Network and Dial-up Connections. The entries in this subkey are written and maintained
 by Group Policy and read and interpreted by the network services programs.

 Entries appear in this subkey when you configure a policy; that is, when you enable or disable the policy.

 Note

 Many of the entries in this subkey have counterparts elsewhere in the registry. These counterparts, known
 as preferences, have the same effect on user or computer features as entries in the Policies subkey.
 However, the entries in the Policies subkey always take precedence over the entries located elsewhere
 in the registry. When an entry appears in the Policies subkey, the preference is ignored.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                   =========                                                    
=================================================== NonEnum ====================================================
                                                   =========                                                    

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\

Description:

 The NonEnum subkey of the Policies subkey contains entries that tell the system not to enumerate (display)
 components of the Windows interface. These entries are written and maintained by Group Policy and read
 and interpreted by the interface programs.

 The Non-Enum policy subkey in HKEY_CURRENT_USER stores entries that are configured separately for each
 user. There is also a Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\NonEnum subkey in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE
 that stores policy-related entries that apply to all users of this computer.

 The entries in this subkey have the following format:

┌───────────────────────────────────┬───────────┬───────┐
│ Class-ID or GUID of the component │ REG-DWORD │ 0 | 1 │
└───────────────────────────────────┴───────────┴───────┘

 Group Policy stores the values of policy settings in this subkey. It adds, deletes, or changes the values
 of entries in this subkey when you configure related Group Policies.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NonEnum subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                              ====================                                              
============================================== NoAddingComponents ==============================================
                                              ====================                                              

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Prevents users from adding Web content to their Active Desktop.

 A value of 1 removes the New button from Web tab in Display in Control Panel and removes the New Desktop
 Item command from the Active Desktop menu. As a result, users cannot add Web pages or pictures from
 the Internet or an intranet to the desktop.

 This entry stores the setting of the Prohibit adding items Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set it to
 Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though the
 value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                   Meaning                                    │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │   The policy is disabled or not configured. Users cann add Web content to    │
│                        │                            their Active desktop.                             │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │ The policy is enabled. Users cannot add Web content to their Active Desktop. │
└────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 This entry does not remove existing Web content from the Active Desktop, or prevent users from removing
 existing Web content.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Prohibit adding items
 policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NoComponents

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||

                                             =====================                                              
============================================= NoChangingWallPaper ==============================================
                                             =====================                                              

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Disables all options on the Background tab of Display in Control Panel. As a result, users cannot add
 or change the background design of the desktop.

 This entry stores the setting of the Disable changing wallpaper Group Policy. Group Policy adds this
 entry to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set
 it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though
 the value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                 Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Options on the Background tab  │
│                        │                               are enabled.                               │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │ The policy is enabled. The Background tab still appears, but all options │
│                        │                         on the tab are disabled.                         │
└────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Disable changing wallpaper
 policy (User Configuration\Administrative Templates\Control Panel\Display).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                             =====================                                              
============================================= NoClosingComponents ==============================================
                                             =====================                                              

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Determines if users are prevented from removing Web content from their Active Desktop.

 Prevents users from closing Web content from their Active Desktop.

 A value of 1 removes the list of the Active Desktop items from the Active Desktop menu. (To see this
 list, right-click the desktop and point to Active Desktop. The list appears at the bottom of the menu.)
 Also, it removes the check boxes from items on the Web tab in Display in Control Panel.

 This entry stores the setting of the Prohibit closing items Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set it to
 Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though the
 value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                   │
├────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Users can close Web content from │
│                        │                           their Active Desktop.                            │
├────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │  The policy is enabled. Users cannot close Web content from their Active   │
│                        │                                  Desktop.                                  │
└────────────────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 In Active Desktop, you can add items to the desktop, but close them so they are not displayed. If you
 set the value of this entry to 1, items added to the desktop cannot be closed; they always appear on
 the desktop.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Prohibit closing items
 policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

 Note

 This entry does not prevent users from deleting items from their Active Desktop.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NoDeletingComponents

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                 ==============                                                 
================================================= NoComponents =================================================
                                                 ==============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Removes Active Desktop content and prevents users from adding Active Desktop content.

 This entry stores the setting of the Disable all items Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry to
 the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set it to Not
 configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though the value
 is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Users can add and remove Active │
│                        │                              Desktop content.                             │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │ The policy is enabled. Active Desktop is removed and users cannot restore │
│                        │                                    it.                                    │
└────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 Setting the value of this entry to 1 removes all Active Desktop items from the desktop. It also removes
 the Web tab from Display in Control Panel and removes the New Desktop Item command from the Active Desktop
 menu. As a result, users cannot add Web pages or pictures from the Internet or an intranet to the desktop.

 This entry does not disable Active Desktop. Users can still use image formats, such as JPEG and GIF,
 for their desktop wallpaper.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Disable all items
 policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

 Note

 To make changes to this entry effective, you must log off of Windows 2000 and then log on again.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NoAddingComponents

 NoDeletingComponents

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                             ======================                                             
============================================= NoDeletingComponents =============================================
                                             ======================                                             

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Prevents users from deleting Web content from their Active Desktop.

 A value of 1 removes the Delete button from the Web tab in Display in Control Panel. As a result, users
 can temporarily remove, but not delete, Web content from their Active Desktop.

 This entry stores the setting of the Prohibit deleting items Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry when you configure the Prohibit deleting items policy.

┌───────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                 Meaning                                  │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │     Users are able to delete Web content from their Active desktop.      │
├───────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │ Users are prevented from deleting Web content from their Active Desktop. │
└───────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 This entry does not prevent users from adding Web content to their Active Desktop.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Prohibit deleting
 items policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NoClosingComponents

 NoComponents

                                             =====================                                              
============================================= NoEditingComponents ==============================================
                                             =====================                                              

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Prevents users from changing the properties of Web content items on their Active Desktop.

 Setting the value of this entry to 1 disables the Properties button on the Web tab in Display in Control
 Panel. Also, it removes the Properties item from the menu for each item on the Active Desktop. As a
 result, users can change the properties of an item, such as its synchronization schedule, password,
 or display characteristics.

 This entry stores the setting of the Prohibit editing items Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set it to
 Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though the
 value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Users can change the properties │
│                        │                  of Web content on their Active Desktop.                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │  The policy is enabled. Users cannot change the properties of Web content │
│                        │                          on their Active Desktop.                         │
└────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Prohibit editing items
 policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

                                               =================                                                
=============================================== NoHTMLWallPaper ================================================
                                               =================                                                

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Permits only bitmap images for wallpaper.

 This entry stores the setting of the Allow only bitmapped wallpaper Group Policy. Group Policy adds this
 entry to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the Allow only bitmapped wallpaper policy. If
 you disable the policy or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry
 and the system behaves as though the value is 0.

┌───────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                 Meaning                                 │
├───────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │  The policy is disabled or not configured. Any image format can be used │
│       │                              for wallpaper.                             │
├───────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │  The policy is enabled. The desktop background ("wallpaper") is limited │
│       │ to bitmap (.bmp) files. If users select files with other image formats, │
│       │      such as JPEG, GIF, PNG, or HTML, the wallpaper does not load.      │
└───────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 This policy is designed to avoid the Active Desktop prompt. When users select a wallpaper with an alternate
 image format, the system prompts them to enable Active Desktop. By limiting users to bitmapped files,
 the prompt is avoided.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Allow only bitmapped
 wallpaper policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

                                                     =====                                                      
===================================================== Add ======================================================
                                                     =====                                                      

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\ActiveDesktop\AdminComponent

┌───────────┬───────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Data type │   Range   │               Default value               │
├───────────┼───────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   REG_SZ  │ URL[ URL] │ There is no default value for this entry. │
└───────────┴───────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘

Description:

 Adds specified Web content items to the desktop, and prevents users from permanently deleting these items.

 Users can close or delete the items (if policies allow), but the items are added again each time the
 policy is refreshed.

 This entry stores the item you type in the Add box of the Add/Delete items Group Policy. Group Policy
 adds this entry to the registry when you enable the Add/Delete items policy. If you disable the policy
 or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Add/Delete items policy
 (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop).

 Note

 Items removed from the value of this entry are not deleted from the desktop. They are just not added
 again if a user deletes them.

 To make changes to this entry effective, you must log off of Windows 2000 and then log on again.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

└───────────┴───────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘

Description:

 Deletes specified Web content items from the desktop.

 Users can add the items again (if policies allow), but the items are deleted each time the policy is
 refreshed.

 This entry stores the item you type in the Delete box of the Add/Delete items Group Policy. Group Policy
 adds this entry to the registry when you enable the Add/Delete items policy. If you disable the policy
 or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Add/Delete items policy
 (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop\Active Desktop). You can also use this policy to
 delete particular Web-based items from users' desktops. Users can add the item again (if policies allow),
 but the item is deleted each time the policy is refreshed.

 Note

 To make changes to this entry effective, you must log off of Windows 2000 and then log on again.

                                                 ==============                                                 
================================================= NoBackButton =================================================
                                                 ==============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Comdlg32

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Removes the Back button from the Open dialog box.

 This entry stores the setting of the Hide the common dialog back button Group Policy. Group Policy adds
 this entry to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or
 set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as
 though the value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                 Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. The Back button appears on the │
│                        │                             Open dialog box.                             │
├────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │  The policy is enabled. The Back button is removed from the Open dialog  │
│                        │                                   box.                                   │
└────────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 This entry, and related entries in this subkey, lets you remove new features added in Windows 2000, so
 that the Open dialog box looks like it did in Windows NT 4.0 and earlier. These entries only affect
 programs that use the standard Open dialog box provided to developers of Windows programs.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Hide the common dialog
 back button policy (User Configuration\Administrative Templates\Windows Components\Windows Explorer\Common
 Open File Dialog).

Tip:

 To see an example of the standard Open dialog box, run Notepad and, from the File menu, click Open.

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                                 ==============                                                 
================================================= ClassicShell =================================================
                                                 ==============                                                 

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Disables Active Desktop, Web view, and thumbnail views. Also, users cannot configure their system to
 open items by single-clicking (such as in Mouse in Control Panel). As a result, the user interface looks
 and operates like the interface for Windows NT 4.0 and users cannot restore the new features.

 This entry stores the setting of the Enable Classic Shell Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable the policy or set it to
 Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system behaves as though the
 value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                   │
├────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. The system displays the new user │
│                        │               interface features designed for Windows 2000.                │
├────────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │  The policy is enabled. The user interface behaves like the interface for  │
│                        │         Windows NT 4.0 and users cannot restore the new features.          │
└────────────────────────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Enable Classic Shell
 policy (User Configuration\Administrative Templates\Windows Components\Windows Explorer).

 Note

 This entry takes precedence over the value of the ForceActiveDesktopOn entry. When the value of ClassicShell
 is 1, Active Desktop is disabled, and ForceActiveDesktopOn is ignored.

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 ForceActiveDesktopOn

 NoActiveDesktop

 NoFolderOptions

//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                            =======================                                             
============================================ ClearRecentDocsOnExit =============================================
                                            =======================                                             

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │      0 0      │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Deletes the contents of the Documents menu when the user logs off.

 The Documents menu contains shortcuts to the non-program files the user opened most recently.

 This entry stores the setting of the Clear history of recently opened documents on exit Group Policy.
 Group Policy adds this entry to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable
 the policy or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system
 behaves as though the value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Shortcuts in the Documents menu │
│                        │  are saved when the user logs off and available again when the user logs  │
│                        │                                    on.                                    │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │  The policy is enabled. The Documents menu is emptied when the user logs  │
│                        │                                    off.                                   │
└────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 You can use the Clear history of recently opened documents on exit policy, in coordination with the Remove
 Documents menu from Start Menu policy (NoRecentDocsMenu) and the Do not keep history of recently opened
 documents policy (NoRecentDocsHistory) to manage access to recently opened files. The system uses this
 entry only when neither of these related entries is set to 1.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Clear history of recently
 opened documents on exit policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Start Menu & Taskbar).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 NoRecentDocsHistory

 NoRecentDocsMenu

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\
|||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
//////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////

                                            ========================                                            
============================================ DisableLocalMachineRun ============================================
                                            ========================                                            

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Directs the system to ignore the customized run list for Windows NT 4.0 and earlier.

 This entry stores the setting of the Disable legacy run list Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you configure the Disable legacy run list policy. If you disable
 the policy or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system
 behaves as though the value is 0.

┌───────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                  Meaning                                   │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Windows 2000 adds any customized │
│       │    run list configured for Windows NT 4.0 and earlier to its run list.     │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │ The policy is enabled. The system ignores the run list for Windows NT 4.0  │
│       │                                and earlier.                                │
└───────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 A run list is customized list of additional programs and documents that the system starts automatically
 when it starts. These programs are added to the standard run list of programs and services that the
 system starts.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Disable legacy run
 list policy (User Configuration\Administrative Templates\System\Logon/Logoff).

 Note

 This entry can appear in both HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE and HKEY_CURRENT_USER. If this entry appears in both
 subtrees, the value in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE takes precedence over the value in HKEY_CURRENT_USER.

Tip:

 The customized run lists for Windows NT 4.0 and earlier are stored in the registry in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run
 and HKEY_CURRENT_USER\Software\Microsoft\Windows NT\CurrentVersion\Windows\Run. They can be configured
 by using the Run policy in System Policy Editor for Windows NT 4.0 and earlier.

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 DisableLocalMachineRun (HKLM)

 DisableLocalMachineRunOnce (HKCU)

 Run subkey (HKLM)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\

                                          ============================                                          

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Directs the system to ignore customized run-once lists.

 This entry stores the setting of the Disable the run once list Group Policy. Group Policy adds this entry
 to the registry with a value of 1 when you configure the Disable the run once list policy. If you disable
 the policy or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system

┌───────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Value │                                Meaning                                 │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   0   │ The policy is disabled or not configured. The system runs the programs │
│       │                         in the run-once list.                          │
├───────┼────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│   1   │      The policy is enabled. The system ignores the run-once list.      │
└───────┴────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 A run-once list is customized list of additional programs and documents that are started automatically
 the next time the system starts (but not thereafter). These programs are added to the standard list
 of programs and services that the system starts.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Disable the run once
 list policy (Computer Configuration\Administrative Templates\System).

 Note

 This entry can appear in both HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE and HKEY_CURRENT_USER. If this entry appears in both
 subtrees, the value in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE takes precedence over the value in HKEY_CURRENT_USER.

Tip:

 Customized run-once lists are stored in the registry in HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\RunOnce.

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.

Related Entries:

 DisableLocalMachineRunOnce (HKLM)

 DisableLocalMachineRun (HKCU)

 Run subkey (HKCU)

\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\

                                           ==========================                                           
=========================================== DisablePersonalDirChange ===========================================
                                           ==========================                                           

 HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\Explorer

┌───────────┬───────┬───────────────┐
│ Data type │ Range │ Default value │
├───────────┼───────┼───────────────┤
│ REG_DWORD │ 0 | 1 │       0       │
└───────────┴───────┴───────────────┘

Description:

 Prevents users from moving the My Documents folder.

 This entry stores the setting of the Prohibit user from changing My Documents path Group Policy. Group
 Policy adds this entry to the registry with a value of 1 when you enable the policy. If you disable
 the policy or set it to Not configured, Group Policy deletes the entry from the registry and the system
 behaves as though the value is 0.

┌────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         Value          │                                  Meaning                                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ 0 (or not in registry) │ The policy is disabled or not configured. Users can move the My Documents │
│                        │                                  folder.                                  │
├────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│           1            │     The policy is enabled. Users cannot move the My Documents folder.     │
└────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

 By default, a user can move the My Documents folder by typing a new path in the Target box of the My
 Documents Properties dialog box. If the value of this entry is 1, then when users type a new path in
 the Target box, a message appears explaining that a policy prevents the action.

Change method:

 To change the value of this entry, use Group Policy. This entry corresponds to the Prohibit user from
 changing My Documents path policy (User Configuration\AdministrativeTemplates\Desktop).

Tip:

 For detailed information about particular Group Policy settings, see the Group Policy Reference (Gp.chm)
 on the Windows 2000 Resource Kit companion CD.

 For general information about Group Policy, see Group Policy in Windows 2000 Help.

 To see a table associating policies with their corresponding registry entries, see the Group Policy Reference
 Table.
